<div id="review_1776429666" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1776429666" />
    <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner"><img alt="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551272804p2/3481302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1776429666?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner">Eon ♒Windrunner♒  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780425240137" href="/book/show/7688834-archangel-s-consort">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1776429666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11855106657363836670">Our MC’s are back from Beijing and recovering from the maelstrom of events that took place, but they are not afforded a breathing chance as vampires are acting strangely all over. Someone or something seems to be influencing their behavior and Elena is immediately called in to investigate when death visits a school in the form of a vampire with bloodlust. Problem is, this seems to be only the beginning with similar incidents taking place all over. And to top it all the unusual behavior is not is</span>
  <span id="freeText11855106657363836670" style="display:none">Our MC’s are back from Beijing and recovering from the maelstrom of events that took place, but they are not afforded a breathing chance as vampires are acting strangely all over. Someone or something seems to be influencing their behavior and Elena is immediately called in to investigate when death visits a school in the form of a vampire with bloodlust. Problem is, this seems to be only the beginning with similar incidents taking place all over. And to top it all the unusual behavior is not isolated to vampires alone as even Archangels seem to be randomly taken by a rage. When the earthquakes and extreme weather rear their ugly head though, everything starts pointing to an ancient story…<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“There is a legend,” Raphael murmured, his wings flaring out as he tugged her into the curve of his body—as if he would protect her. “That mountains will shake and rivers overflow, while ice creeps across the world and fields drown in rain.” He looked down her at, his eyes that impossible, inhuman chrome blue. “All this will come to pass ... when an Ancient awakens.”<br />The chill in his tone raised every hair on her body.</i>
</b><br /><br />There are many stories about the ancients, the ones who sleep. No-one knows how many of them there are, but there have been disappearances throughout time. And now it seems one of them is waking, one who was possibly insane before she disappeared, one who may be more powerful than any other…<br /><br />Raphael, Elena and his Seven need to do everything in their power to find this ancient one’s resting place in order to determine the threat posed and what can be done, but they are not the only ones seeking this ancient being. Before this is over, they will come to encounter an evil heretofore unbeknownst to them. And the bonds that tie Raphael and Elena together will be tested beyond anything they have known before.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“We fall, we fall together.”</i>
</b><br /><br />The story is well written, fascinating and hot. Nalini Singh is similarly adept at portraying the nuances and depths of emotion that make up the complex relationships her characters develop with each other as she is at creating vast and intricate worlds with compelling histories and engrossing cultures. If you love paranormal romance but are yet to read this author, you are, without a doubt, missing out. While this is not my preferred genre, I am thoroughly enjoying it and more than happy that I am part of this BB&amp;B buddy read. Thank you for asking me to read it with you Jo :D<br /><br />Two thumbs up to Nalini Singh.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1755604474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1755604474" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1755604474?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-print">books-i-own-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-kindle">books-i-own-kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1755604474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8732310599271231609"><b>1st Read - April 2013</b><br/><b>2nd Read - September 2016</b><br/><b>3rd Read - September 2020</b><br/><br/><b>Original Review</b><br/><br/>It is time for Vampire Hunter Elena to return to New York and let the world see the changes she has gone through but as nothing ever goes smoothly for the couple they soon find themselves caught up in the hunt of their lives. As more and more vampires are taken over by bloodlust they quickly realise that all is not what it seems, a powerful enemy is rising, a face from Raphael's past that he hoped never to see </span>
  <span id="freeText8732310599271231609" style="display:none"><b>1st Read - April 2013</b><br /><b>2nd Read - September 2016</b><br /><b>3rd Read - September 2020</b><br /><br /><b>Original Review</b><br /><br />It is time for Vampire Hunter Elena to return to New York and let the world see the changes she has gone through but as nothing ever goes smoothly for the couple they soon find themselves caught up in the hunt of their lives. As more and more vampires are taken over by bloodlust they quickly realise that all is not what it seems, a powerful enemy is rising, a face from Raphael's past that he hoped never to see again and one who is determined to get Elena out of the way. Even working together this enemy may be too strong for them, their only hope is to defeat them before they regain their full power but that would mean breaking one of the most ancient angelic laws.<br /><br />I'm a huge fan of this series and I really enjoyed this instalment of Elena and Raphael's adventures. Elena is still coming to grips with her immortality and the new abilities she gained when she became an angel. Although she is stronger and heals faster than she ever did as a human she is still weak compared to other angels and even the older vampires who protect Raphael. She is determined to train as hard as possible though because she doesn't want to be seen as Raphael's weakness but anyone who knows how much he cares for her automatically sees her as a target. It isn't easy for her to adjust to her new life, she is still learning the rules and learning what her body is now capable of but she is just as brave and determined as she ever was. She may be weaker than her enemies but she refuses to back down and wants to stand by Raphael. The two of them will always be stronger together than they are separately and I love that although they are both uncertain when it comes to relationships and find it difficult to trust they work together to overcome their issues.<br /><br />We learn a lot more about both of their pasts in this book and discover a lot about their families that make us question things we thought we already knew. Elena has always had a very poor relationship with her father (I can't stand the man!) but although they are a long way from a close father / daughter relationship we do see a glimmer of hope that he isn't all bad. One new thing that Elena has to contend with though is the mother-in-law from hell, seriously if you think your MIL is bad she's got nothing on Caliane! Of course Elena isn't going to put up with crap from anyone and there are some really amusing moments where she stands up for both herself and Raphael. We already knew that Raphael didn't have the best relationship with his mother but what we find out about his past is heartbreaking and goes a long way to explaining why he is so closed off to the people around him. He is lucky to have his Seven to rely on but it is Elena who has really started to bring him out of himself. Raphael has changed so much from when we first met him, he is still dangerous and he still scares the crap out of me sometimes but he can also be so unbelievably sweet and protective over Elena. Their relationship has come on leaps and bounds since they first met but they still have their ups and downs, they have to work hard and find ways to compromise so that they can both be happy but they are both willing to put the effort in.<br /><br />Archangel's Consort is just as sexy as the first two books in the series, there is no missing the fireworks when Raphael and Elena are in the same room, but there is also a deeper connection between them now that wasn't there in the beginning. We are also getting to learn more about Raphael's Seven and I can't wait to spend more time with each of them. Illium is a particular favourite of mine and I really hope he gets a book of his own at some point but even Dimitri and Venom are growing on me now that I know them better. Alongside the hot sex and great character development Nalini Singh has created a fast moving plot that had me gripping the pages. I didn't want the story to end and I'm just relieved that I already have the next book waiting for me to read it. This remains one of my favourite paranormal series and I don't see that changing any time soon.<br /><br />________________<br /><br /><b>2nd Read</b><br /><br />Buddy read with Aly, Ange &amp; Maru<br /><br />I'm totally addicted and loving this series even more the second time around.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8732310599271231609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44132489-mindy-lou-s-book-review?shelf=my-kind-of-alpha">my-kind-of-alpha</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44132489-mindy-lou-s-book-review?shelf=only-sees-h">only-sees-h</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44132489-mindy-lou-s-book-review?shelf=pnr-scifi-fantasy">pnr-scifi-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2976458754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8690589036771974226">This is a pretty addictive series. Raphael and Elena's relationship is one of my favorite kind to read about. Raphael is the big, bad, I-can-kill-all, kind of Angel. Elena is no longer human but she is basically a baby Angel. While she's one of the best vampire hunters, she's still more weak and vulnerable in this supernatural world. <br/><br/>Raphael is still cold and distant but you can see his love for Elena very clearly. He is very protective of her and puts her above all others. She's had fear of him</span>
  <span id="freeText8690589036771974226" style="display:none">This is a pretty addictive series. Raphael and Elena's relationship is one of my favorite kind to read about. Raphael is the big, bad, I-can-kill-all, kind of Angel. Elena is no longer human but she is basically a baby Angel. While she's one of the best vampire hunters, she's still more weak and vulnerable in this supernatural world. <br /><br />Raphael is still cold and distant but you can see his love for Elena very clearly. He is very protective of her and puts her above all others. She's had fear of him in the beginning but that has never stopped herself from fighting back with him. She fell just as hard for him as he had for her. Addictive.<br /><br />Each book seem to start right where the last one leaves off. In Archangel's Consort, Raphael's mom is waking from sleep and causing all kinds of havoc. They learn pretty quickly that she does not approve of Elena. Typical mother-in-law right there. Caliane was already considered mad before she disappeared and now she will be even stronger. Raphael must make a choice about whether she should live or die.</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1938504644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13520159346680786647">OK. Wow, so I’m officially on the Guild Hunter train. <br/><br/>When I read the 1st book a year ago, I was feeling somewhat lukewarm, and then, by the 2nd book, I started truly enjoying it. <b>This book, however, has me realize how much I appreciate the author’s craft: the world-building, the plot, the characters – I love it.</b><br/><br/>The plot is more on the slow side, but for once, I am actually totally OK with that. <b>There is a nice gradual build-up to every development in the plot and characters.</b> It is fun discoveri</span>
  <span id="freeText13520159346680786647" style="display:none">OK. Wow, so I’m officially on the Guild Hunter train. <br /><br />When I read the 1st book a year ago, I was feeling somewhat lukewarm, and then, by the 2nd book, I started truly enjoying it. <b>This book, however, has me realize how much I appreciate the author’s craft: the world-building, the plot, the characters – I love it.</b><br /><br />The plot is more on the slow side, but for once, I am actually totally OK with that. <b>There is a nice gradual build-up to every development in the plot and characters.</b> It is fun discovering and learning something new about this world and its people. In addition, I love the romance because it’s just so sweet and thoughtful and good! <b>The huge emphasis on mutual respect has my heart sighing contently. </b><br /><br />I think it has helped me to thoroughly enjoy this book – page by page – by spreading it across 2 months (not intentionally 2 months, but it just happened that way). I did not read it every single day, but the urge would strike me every few days, and I would sometimes read a few pages or a few chapters, depending on my mood. Overall, I give <i>Archangel’s Consort (Guild Hunter #3)</i> <b>4 stars</b>. My feelings for this book have certainly shifted since the 1st book and the 2nd book. I am excited to see what happens next (6 more books to go at the moment?)~<br /><br /><u>Things that you might want to know <b>(WARNING: Spoilers below)</b></u><br />Is there a happy/satisfying ending? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Happy, but cliffhanger-ish because it’s not the last book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Love triangle? Cheating? Angst level? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No, no, low-ish. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Tears-worthy? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It could get emotional, but not a depressing book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Humor? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Not really. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Favorite scene? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tbh, any Raphael and Elena scene. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />What age level would be appropriate? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mature audience. There are: explicit details on sex, PTSD, there are some horrific, bloody moments, deaths, etc. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />-------<br /><br />I haven't continued this series in monthsssss, and I sorta-kinda miss it now.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10652538117747335898">
  <br/>
  <a href='http://s39.photobucket.com/user/phoenix374/media/9875509_zpsbrn9ysqv.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444558025i/16516992.jpg' alt=' photo 9875509_zpsbrn9ysqv.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>

<br/><br/><b><br/><br/>Swathed in the silken shadows of the deepest night, New York was the same . . . and altered beyond compare. <br/>Elena and Raphael are back in New York. Elena is still trying to adjust to her wings to becoming stronger and to dealing with mortality or immortality. But throughout other things are stirring. Weather patterns are changing and a lot of the Cadre are becoming even more unpredictable than before. There is once again no rest for the wicked as there are more murders to solve</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10652538117747335898" style="display:none">
  <br>
  <a href="http://s39.photobucket.com/user/phoenix374/media/9875509_zpsbrn9ysqv.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444558025i/16516992.jpg" alt=" photo 9875509_zpsbrn9ysqv.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
  <br>
<br><br><b><br><br>Swathed in the silken shadows of the deepest night, New York was the same . . . and altered beyond compare. <br>Elena and Raphael are back in New York. Elena is still trying to adjust to her wings to becoming stronger and to dealing with mortality or immortality. But throughout other things are stirring. Weather patterns are changing and a lot of the Cadre are becoming even more unpredictable than before. There is once again no rest for the wicked as there are more murders to solve that leads Raphael to believe that an Ancient is awaking. I mean give the poor angel a break Elena soon as a mother in law to contend with and that isn’t going to be easy.<br>We get more background on Elena’s family and where the hunter gene truly comes from and that there are other hidden secrets as well. His sister Eve is also hunter born. <br>I love Ms. Singh’s writing and the world that she has created it has been created with such ease that I just can’t get enough it is like coming home. I love the secondary characters especially Bluebell but Dimitri and Venom have also grown on me as well. This is a series that I can read over and over again. <br>Reading this for the second time I have to say that although I did day that it is my least favorite in the series l have bumped it up from 3 Stars to 4 Stars.</b></span>

<div id="review_172812775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172812775" />
    <a title="Anzu The Great Destroyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer"><img alt="Anzu The Great Destroyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455829739p2/2278800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172812775?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anzu The Great Destroyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anzu The Great Destroyer" href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer">Anzu The Great Destroyer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9875509-archangel-s-consort">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who still fall for the caveman attitude</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=lots-of-mushy-stuff">lots-of-mushy-stuff</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=facepalm">facepalm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=suburban-fantasy">suburban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=fanged-and-deadly">fanged-and-deadly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=is-it-just-me-goddammit">is-it-just-me-goddammit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=dat-cover-goddammit">dat-cover-goddammit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=romance-paranormal">romance-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=could-have-been-sooo-much-better">could-have-been-sooo-much-better</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172812775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5284614143819456227">I'm re-reading this series. The latest installment is out so I want to be in the zone. But oh wow. This is awkward. I could not finish it.<br/><br/>I COULD NOT FUCKING FINISH IT.<br/><br/>And I used to love it. I used to love it a lot. People change. Indeed they do.<br/><br/>What made me feel this way? There's no fucking story. It's all about Raphael banging Elena, Elena banging Raphael and so on. I also have a big problem with Raphael's caveman attitude. Nope, cannot stand it. <br/><br/>So that's it for me. I'm dropping the series. S</span>
  <span id="freeText5284614143819456227" style="display:none">I'm re-reading this series. The latest installment is out so I want to be in the zone. But oh wow. This is awkward. I could not finish it.<br><br>I COULD NOT FUCKING FINISH IT.<br><br>And I used to love it. I used to love it a lot. People change. Indeed they do.<br><br>What made me feel this way? There's no fucking story. It's all about Raphael banging Elena, Elena banging Raphael and so on. I also have a big problem with Raphael's caveman attitude. Nope, cannot stand it. <br><br>So that's it for me. I'm dropping the series. Sad, but not really.<br><br><br>------------------<br>Old review:<br><br>September 6th 2011… now that’s cruel if you ask me. *sighs* And so ends the final book in my Guild Hunter collection. I have two short stories that I need to read but it’s still not the same thing… total sadness… *dramatic music playing in the background * The HORROR!!!! *shakes fist in the air*<br><br>Now that I’m done with that breakdown I’ll continue my review. Excuse my outburst…<br><br>So, we start with an annoying Raphael. I really don’t know wtf was wrong with him at the beginning of the book but I was pretty sure their relationship would get maimed somehow. Just check out this quote:<br><br><i>“I was worried about you.”<br>‹I am an archangel.›<br>Unsaid were the words that he found the worry of a woman who’d been mortal not long ago—who was still not a true immortal—laughable.</i><br><br>Wtf again! I mean you go through so much shit to be together and now you take this asshole attitude. Where’s a baseball bat when you need one…<br><br>If this crap Raphael was giving would have lasted till the middle of the book, or something like this, I would have given it a bad review. Yep, that’s the sad, very sad truth. But of course the wonderful Nalini Singh wouldn’t do this to us. *eyes sparkle with awe* By the end of the book the change in Raphael is so huge (heh, pun intended – if you know what I mean) that he seems a totally different pers- eeerr… archangel… Sooo happy day for a problem solved! Wilson, you may serve the tea and crackers!<br><br>Some of you may have booed the book because of the pretty huge (heeh, can’t get enough of this) amount of sex scenes it has. Yes, you may be right. But I know you’re all perverts and you enjoyed each second of it. So suck it up and quit whining! It’s just the couple’s way of letting out steam. So yeah, therapy. That’s the way you should see it. Looooong sweaty sexy therapy. The best there ever was.<br><br>My favorite scene, or maybe one of my favorites, is where Elena spars with Raphael. I always found fighting, or sparring as you wish to put it, between lovers erotic. Wish I could do that myself one day. But first I have to get some lessons. Which is also sexy if the tutor is a hottie. I guess I can go on with this all day so I’ll just stop here. *coughs* Uhm so yes, sparring… sexy… moving on… *wipes her forehead*<br><br>The story itself was really great, loved the fact that the enemy is someone with a colossal amount of power. And Raphael’s mum. That’s just freaky if you ask me. I always knew mum-in-laws had problems with their sons’ wives, or whatever, but come on! Imagine dating Raphael and one day having dinner with Caliane. That’s nightmare material if you ask me. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380350785i/704539._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The city is in ruins – nah scratch that! The world is in ruins. Chaos everywhere. Vamps going crazy, you don’t know who’s sane and who’s not anymore. The end is uncertain. And I loved it all. I can’t say it’s as good as the previous books, but this series can easily be called a masterpiece. And also Elena and Raphael are one of the best couples ever created. Their little (heh – it was huge *grins*) angel dance was interesting. I must admit I was expecting something else so I can’t form an opinion about this. I won’t look at the world with the same eyes anymore *sad music playing in the background* <br><br>I’ve missed Michaela’s death in the book. Since it didn’t happen so far I’m sure Nalini Singh has something special hidden somewhere for her. I’m still hoping it involves lots of pain and torture but I doubt it. *looks towards the sky* WHY?!?! Why must she live?!?!?!<br><br>Wilson! Bring me my secret-kill-Michaela-in-the-next-book plan! <br><br>Yeeees!!! *pats the folder* Soon my precious…<br><br>Now, to prove my point of how this epic the book is, I will just paste a simple scene. No spoilers, nothing to ruin the mood. This is one of the reasons why Nalini Singh grew on me so much.<br><br><i>She was hunter-born, could handle vampires twice her size without blinking. The crowd might overpower her, but not before she took down a significant percentage of their number. Noting that the walls of humanity had blocked all other traffic on both ends of the street, she walked to stand in the middle . . . and looked up at the sky. And there he was, his wingspan creating a massive shadow as he swept down to land in front of her. “Are you well, Consort?”<br>Silence held their audience in thrall, their awe now licked with dread. “They’re only curious.” She saw the danger in his eyes, knew he had the capacity to execute every human on the street. “I should’ve considered it. I just ... forgot that nothing’s the same anymore.”</i><br><br>How can you not love it?!?! Seriously!<br><br><b>Top five quotes:</b><br><b>#5</b><i> “A lot of women have trouble with their mothers-in-law.”<br>Raphael’s look was priceless. “My mother is an insane archangel.”</i><br><br><b>#4</b><i> He was an archangel. He’d been wounded far, far worse and shrugged it off. But then, there had been no woman with skin kissed by the sunset and eyes of storm gray to tear into him for daring to get himself hurt.</i><br><br><b>#3</b><i> Elena.<br>Hush, let me talk to the crazy lady.</i><br><br><b>#2</b><i>“Death holds no allure for me, Elena.” The power of him cut against his skin, a cold white fire. “Not when I have yet to sate my hunger for you.”</i><br><br><b>#1</b><i>“Raphael, tell him you won’t do anything to him if I get ‘damaged.’ ”<br>“That would be a lie, Elena. I would tear out his throat.”</i><br><br>Read the review on <a href="http://zombiehazard.blogspot.com/2011/06/archangel-consort-guild-hunter-3.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"></a>ZombieHazard.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5284614143819456227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_100457903" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100457903" />
    <a title="valee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2320890-valee"><img alt="valee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443365004p2/2320890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100457903?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="valee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="valee" href="/user/show/2320890-valee">valee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2320890-valee?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100457903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9013061360329693015"><b>OMFG, and to believe I was afraid I would not like it as much as the first 2 books</b>. I have no idea how so many rated this book lower than those because for me it was way better than book 2. I loved it, absolutely adored it. I had been waiting to read anything about this series for so long, and to finally be able to do so was amazing, better than everything I could have ever expected. So many things happened in this book, many all time changing events, and I can't wait to read how everything will</span>
  <span id="freeText9013061360329693015" style="display:none"><b>OMFG, and to believe I was afraid I would not like it as much as the first 2 books</b>. I have no idea how so many rated this book lower than those because for me it was way better than book 2. I loved it, absolutely adored it. I had been waiting to read anything about this series for so long, and to finally be able to do so was amazing, better than everything I could have ever expected. So many things happened in this book, many all time changing events, and I can't wait to read how everything will turn out now. There better be one more book about this couple before NS starts with Raphael's seven because I definitely haven't had enough of this 2. This is one of the best UF series there is out there, I love every book in it and if there where more books in it I know I would be even more obsessed. <br /><br />NS is definitely one of the best writers and knows how to get you hooked right away. I always find myself trapped in the pages and can't put down her books, it feels as if you were watching a movie and you just can't pause, not even to go to the bathroom because it is THAT addictive. **SIGH**, now one more year to read more about this amazing characters, not fair, I need more NOW!!! I still have to find a book from this author which is not absolutely fantastic.<br /><br />In this installment we see so much more about our amazing couple that it will make you go crazy. I loved this book so much because while in the first 2 installments we saw a lot of this couple I always had the feeling it wasn't enough. Well, let me tell you that THAT will never happen to you on this book because you definitely read everything, and I mean EVERYTHING, there is to know about this 2 in here. And it was everything I wanted it to be. They make such an amazing couple and you never get tired of getting to know more about them or seeing them together. Their love just feels right, PERFECT. They are one of my top fav couples and I need more from them still. I believe they can become much powerful than they already are and that reading about it will be amazing. I just can't wait for the next books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9013061360329693015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7247640-kira"><img alt="Kira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395614362p2/7247640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344421330?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kira" href="/user/show/7247640-kira">Kira</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780425240137" href="/book/show/7688834-archangel-s-consort">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=angels">angels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344421330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18405913127832081721">June 8, 2012: 3 stars<br/>Oct. 10, 2016: 4 stars<br/><br/>I think the reason I like these so much better the second time around is because I’m not reading them back to back. Elena’s flashbacks aren’t as bothersome when there is some time between books. I had been really irritated with them the first time because they were repetitive with so little new info learned from them. <br/><br/>The plot was weak. Elena and Raphael were dealing with personal issues and some of the weird stuff that was going on, but for most of the</span>
  <span id="freeText18405913127832081721" style="display:none">June 8, 2012: 3 stars<br />Oct. 10, 2016: 4 stars<br /><br />I think the reason I like these so much better the second time around is because I’m not reading them back to back. Elena’s flashbacks aren’t as bothersome when there is some time between books. I had been really irritated with them the first time because they were repetitive with so little new info learned from them. <br /><br />The plot was weak. Elena and Raphael were dealing with personal issues and some of the weird stuff that was going on, but for most of the book there wasn’t an imminent mystery to be solved. I was okay with it because learning more about Elena and Raphael’s family history was interesting. There were a few unexpected twists. <br /><br />Elena and Raphael are different as a couple. Something about their relationship feels real. They have a great connect, yet there is still a lot of insecurity. Unlike other PNR novels they didn’t fall in love and have everything in their relationship fall perfectly into place. Things are complicated between them because they come from totally different worlds. They are too forgiving of their differences sometimes but it is a novel. <br /><br />With the way this book ended, it is weird that the next book is not a continuation of their story. It wasn’t a cliffhanger, but there was a revelation that needs further explanation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18405913127832081721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_119268673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119268673" />
    <a title="Gianne Kris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4223632-gianne-kris"><img alt="Gianne Kris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298985950p2/4223632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119268673?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gianne Kris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gianne Kris" href="/user/show/4223632-gianne-kris">Gianne Kris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6170653433215235775">Advance Excerpt from Archangel's Consort<br/><br/>Chapter 1<br/><br/>Swathed in the silken shadows of deepest night, New York was the same . . . and altered beyond compare. Once Elena had watched angels take flight from the light-filled column of the Tower as she sat in front of the distant window of her cherished apartment. Now, she was one of those angels, perched high atop a balcony that had no railing, nothing to prevent a deadly fall.<br/><br/>Except of course, she would no longer fall.<br/><br/>Her wings were stronger now.   <span id="freeText6170653433215235775" style="display:none">Advance Excerpt from Archangel's Consort<br /><br />Chapter 1<br /><br />Swathed in the silken shadows of deepest night, New York was the same . . . and altered beyond compare. Once Elena had watched angels take flight from the light-filled column of the Tower as she sat in front of the distant window of her cherished apartment. Now, she was one of those angels, perched high atop a balcony that had no railing, nothing to prevent a deadly fall.<br /><br />Except of course, she would no longer fall.<br /><br />Her wings were stronger now. She was stronger.<br /><br />Flaring out those wings, she took a deep breath of the air of home. A fusion of scents--spice and smoke, human and vampire, earthy and sophisticated--hit her with the wild fever of a welcoming rainstorm. Her chest, tight for so long, relaxed, and she stretched her wings out to their greatest width. It was time to explore this familiar place become foreign, this home that was suddenly new again.<br /><br />Diving down from the balcony, she swept across Manhattan on air currents kissed by the cool bite of spring. The bright green season had thawed the snows that had kept the city in thrall this winter, and now held court, summer not even a peach-colored blush on the horizon. This was the time of rebirth, of blooming things and baby birds, bright and young and fragile even in the frenetic rush of a city that never slept.<br /><br />Home. I'm home.<br /><br />Letting the air currents sweep her where they would above the diamond-studded lights of the city, she tested her wings, tested her strength.<br /><br />Stronger.<br /><br />But still weak. An immortal barely-Made.<br /><br />One whose heart remained painfully mortal.<br /><br />So it was no surprise when she found herself trying to hover outside the plate-glass window of her apartment. She didn't yet have the skill to execute the maneuver, and she kept dropping, then having to pull herself back up with fast wingbeats. Still, she saw enough in those fleeting glimpses to know that while the once-shattered glass had been flawlessly repaired, the rooms were empty.<br /><br />There wasn't even a bloodstain on the carpet to mark the spot where she'd spilled Raphael's blood, where she'd tried to staunch the crimson river until her fingers were the same murderous shade.<br /><br />Elena.<br /><br />The scent of the wind and the rain, fresh and wild, around her, inside her, and then strong hands on her hips as Raphael held her effortlessly in position so she could look her fill through the window, her hands flat on the glass.<br /><br />Emptiness.<br /><br />No sign remained of the home she'd created piece by precious piece.<br /><br />"You must teach me how to hover," she said, forcing herself to speak past the knot of loss. It was just a place. Just things. "It'll be a very good way to spy on potential targets."<br /><br />"I intend to teach you many things." Tugging her back against his body, her wings trapped in between, the Archangel of New York pressed his lips to the tip of her ear. "You are full of sorrow."<br /><br />It was instinct to lie, to protect herself, but they'd gone beyond that, she and her archangel. "I guess I somehow expected my apartment to still be here. Sara didn't say anything when she sent me my things." And her best friend had never lied to her.<br /><br />"It was as you left it when Sara visited," Raphael said, drawing back enough that she could flare out her wings and angle her body into the air currents once again. Come, I have something to show you.<br /><br />The words were in her mind, along with the wind and the rain. She didn't order him to get out--because she knew he wasn't in it. This, the way she could sense him so deeply, speak to him with such ease, was part of whatever it was that tied them to one another . . . that taut, twisting emotion that ripped away old scars and created new vulnerabilities in a whip of fire across the soul.<br /><br />But as she watched him fly through the lush black of the sky high over the glittering city, her archangel with his wings of white-gold and eyes of endless, relentless blue, she wasn't sorry. She didn't want to turn back the clock, didn't want to return to a life in which she'd never been held in the arms of an archangel, never felt her heart tear open and reform into something stronger, capable of such furies of emotion that it scared her at times. Where are you taking me, Archangel?<br /><br />Patience, Guild Hunter.<br /><br />She smiled, her grief at the loss of her apartment buried under a wave of amusement. No matter how many times he decreed that her loyalty was now to the angels and not to the Hunters' Guild, he kept betraying how he saw her--as a hunter, as a warrior. Shooting down below him, she dove then rose through the biting freshness of the air with hard, strong wingbeats. Her back and shoulder muscles protested the acrobatics, but she was having too much fun to worry--she'd pay for it in a few hours, no doubt about it, but for now, she felt free and protected in the dark.<br /><br />"Do you think anyone is watching?" she asked, breathless from the exertion, once they were side by side once more.<br /><br />"Perhaps. But the darkness will conceal your identity for the moment."<br /><br />Tomorrow, she knew, when light broke, the circus would begin. An angel-Made . . . Even the oldest of vampires and the angels themselves found her a curiosity. She had no doubts about how the human population would react. "Can't you do your scary thing and make them keep their distance?" However, even as she spoke, she knew it wasn't the reaction of the general population that worried her.<br /><br />Her father . . . No. She wouldn't think about Jeffrey. Not tonight.<br /><br />As she forced away thoughts of the man who had repudiated her when she'd been barely eighteen, Raphael swept out over the Hudson, dropping so hard and fast that she yelped before she could catch herself. The Archangel of New York was one hell of a flier--he skimmed along the water until he could've trailed his fingers in its rushing cold, before pulling himself up in a steep ascent. Showing off.<br /><br />For her.<br /><br />It made her heart lighten, her lips curve.<br /><br />Dipping down to join him at a lower altitude, she watched the night winds whip that sleek ebony hair across his face, as if they could not resist touching him.<br /><br />It will do no good.<br /><br />"What?" Fascinated by the almost cruel beauty of him, this male she dared call her lover, she'd forgotten what she'd asked him.<br /><br />For me to scare them away--you are not a woman to stay in seclusion.<br /><br />"Damn. You're right." Feeling her shoulder muscles begin to pull in ominous warning, she winced. "I think I need to set down soon." Her body had been damaged in the fight against Lijuan. Not much--and the injuries had healed, but the enforced rest period meant she'd lost some of the muscle she'd built up prior to the battle that had turned Beijing into a crater, its voice the silent cry of the dead.<br /><br />We're almost home.<br /><br />Concentrating on keeping herself going in a straight line, she realized he'd shifted position so she was effectively riding his wake--meaning she no longer had to make as much effort to hold herself aloft. Pride had her scrunching her face into a scowl, but contrasting with that was a deep warmth that came from knowing she was important, more than important, to Raphael.<br /><br />And then she saw it, the sprawling mansion that was Raphael's clifftop home on the other side of the river. Though the land backed up against the Hudson, the place was hidden from casual view by a thick verge of trees. However, they were coming at it from above, and from there it looked like a jewel set in the velvet darkness, warm golden light in every window--turning into pulses of color where it hit the clean lines of the stained glass on one side of the building. The rose bushes weren't visible from this angle, but she knew they were there, their leaves luxuriant and glossy against the elegant white of the house, hundreds of buds ready to bloom in a profusion of color as the weather grew warmer.<br /><br />She followed Raphael down as he landed in the yard, the light from the stained glass turning his wings into a kaleidoscope of wild blue, crystalline green, and ruby red. You could've landed on one of the balconies , she said, too focused on ensuring a good landing to speak the words aloud.<br /><br />Raphael didn't disagree, waiting until she was on the ground beside him to say, "I could have." Reaching out as she folded away her wings, he gripped her gently at the curve where her neck flowed into her shoulder, his fingers pressing into the sensitive inner seam of her right wing. "But then your lips would not have been so very close to mine."<br /><br />Her toes curled as he tugged her forward, pleasure blooming in her stomach. "Not here," she murmured, voice husky. "I don't want to shock Jeeves."<br /><br />Raphael kissed away her words with a slow thoroughness that had her forgetting all about his butler, her body warming with a slow, luscious sense of anticipation. Raphael.<br /><br />You tremble, Elena. You are tired.<br /><br />Never too tired for your touch. It terrified her how addicted she'd become to him. The only thing that made it bearable was that his hunger, too, was a raw, near-violent craving.<br /><br />A lick of storm against her senses before he drew back with a hotly sexual promise. Later. A slow, intimate stroke along the upper curve of her wing. I would take my time with you. His lips parted, his spoken words far less incendiary. "Montgomery will like having you for his mistress, Elena."<br /><br />She licked her lips, tried to breathe--and heard the rapid tattoo of her heart against her ribs. Yeah, the archangel knew how to kiss. "Why?" she finally managed to say, falling into step beside him as he walked to the door.<br /><br />"You're likely to get dirty and destroy your clothes on a regular basis." Raphael's humor was dry, his voice an exquisite caress in the night. "It is the same reason he likes it when Illium occasionally stays here. You both give him plenty to do."<br /><br />She made a face at him, but her lips kicked up at the corners. "Is Illium coming to join us?" The blue-winged angel was part of Raphael's Seven, the vampires and angels who had given their loyalty to the Archangel of New York--even to the extent of placing his life before their own. Illium was the only one of the Seven who saw her human heart not as a weakness, but as a gift. And in him, she saw a kind of innocence that had been lost in the other immortals.<br /><br />The door opened at that moment to expose the beaming face of Raphael's butler. "Sire," he said in a plummy English accent she was certain could turn cold and intimidating on command. "It is good to have you home."<br /><br />"Montgomery." Raphael placed a hand on the vampire's shoulder as he passed.<br /><br />Elena smiled at the butler, delighted by him all over again. "Hello."<br /><br />"Mistress."<br /><br />She blinked. "Elena," she said firmly. "I'm no one's mistress but my own." Then there was the fact that though he chose to work in the service of an archangel, Montgomery was a strong vampire, hundreds of years old.<br /><br />The butler's spine went stiff as a board, his eyes shooting to Raphael--who gave a languid smile. "You must not shock Montgomery so, Elena." Reaching out to take her hand, he tugged her to his side. "Perhaps you will allow him to call you Guild Hunter?"<br /><br />Elena looked up, certain the archangel was laughing. But his expression was clear, his lips set with their familiar sensual grace. "Um, yes, okay." She nodded at Montgomery, then felt compelled to ask, "Will that do?"<br /><br />"Of course, Guild Hunter." He gave a small bow. "I was not sure if you would wish a meal, Sire, but I have sent a small tray up to your rooms."<br /><br />"That will be all for tonight, Montgomery."<br /><br />As the butler whispered away, Elena looked with growing suspicion at a large Chinese vase in one corner of the hall, opposite the stained glass wall beside the door. It was decorated with a pattern of sunflowers that seemed oddly familiar. Letting go of Raphael's hand, she stepped closer . . . closer. Her eyes went wide. "This is mine!" Given as a gift by an angel in China after Elena completed a particularly dangerous hunt, one that had taken her into the bowels of the Shanghai underworld.<br /><br />Raphael touched his fingers to the small of her back, a searing brand. "All of your things are here." He waited until she looked up before saying, "They were moved to this house for safekeeping until your return.<br /><br />"However," he continued when she remained silent, her throat a knot of emotion, "it seems Montgomery could not help himself when it came to this vase. I'm afraid he has a weakness for beautiful things and has been known to relocate an item if he feels it is not being accorded the proper appreciation. Once, he 'relocated' an ancient sculpture from the home of another archangel."<br /><br />Elena stared down the corridor where the butler had disappeared in refined silence. "I don't believe you. He's too prim and proper." It was easier to say that, to focus on the humor, than to accept the tightness in her chest, the feelings locking up her throat.<br /><br />"You would be surprised." Touching her lower back again, he nudged her down the hall and up a flight of stairs. "Come, you can look at your belongings in the morning."<br /><br />She dragged her feet at the top of the staircase. "No."<br /><br />Raphael measured her expression with those eyes no mortal would ever possess, a silent visual reminder that he had never been human, would never be anything close to mortal. "Such will." Leading her to a room that flowed off what she knew to be the master bedroom, he opened the door.<br /><br />Everything from her apartment lay neatly stacked, slipcovers over the furnishings, her knickknacks in boxes.<br /><br />She froze on the doorstep, uncertain how she felt--relief and anger and joy all battled for space inside of her. She'd known she could never go back to the apartment that had been her haven, and more, a furious rebuttal against her father's abandonment. The place wasn't built for a being with wings--but the loss had hurt. So much.<br /><br />Now . . . "Why?"<br /><br />His hand closed around her nape with no attempt to hide the possession inherent in the act. "You are mine, Elena. If you choose to sleep in another bed, I will simply pick you up and bring you home."<br /><br />Arrogant words. But he was an archangel. And she'd made a claim of her own. "As long as you remember that goes both ways."<br /><br />Acknowledged, Guild Hunter. A kiss pressed to the curve of her shoulder, his fingers tightening on her nape just a fraction. Come to bed.<br /><br />Arousal kicked her hard, her body knowing full well what pleasure awaited her at those strong, lethal hands. "So we can talk knives and sheaths?"<br /><br />Sensual male laughter, another kiss, the caress of teeth. But he released his hold, watching in silence as she stepped into the room and lifted a slipcover to run her fingers over the delicately embroidered comforter on the bed that had been her own, before she moved to explore the vanity with its store of pretty glass bottles and brushes set tidily inside a small box. She felt like a child, wanting to reassure herself that everything was here, the need visceral enough to hurt.<br /><br />As she gave in to the emotional hunger, her mind disgorged images of another homecoming, of the shock and humiliation that had burned her throat when she'd found her things piled up like so much garbage on the street. Nothing would ever erase that hurt, the pain of the knowledge that that was exactly what she was to her father, but tonight, Raphael had crushed the memory under the weight of a far more powerful act.<br /><br />She had no illusions about her archangel, knew he'd done it in part precisely for the reason he'd given her--so she wouldn't be tempted to treat her apartment as a bolt-hole. But had that been his sole motivation, he could as easily have sent her stuff to the dump. Instead, every single piece had been packed with care and moved here. Some of it had been exposed to the elements when her window shattered that night, and yet now looked pristine, speaking of meticulous restoration.<br /><br />Heart aching at the wonder of being so cherished, she said, "We can go now." She'd come back later, decide what to do with everything. "Raphael--thank you."<br /><br />The brush of his wing against her own, a silent tenderness as they entered the master suite. No one else ever saw this part of him, she thought, eyes on her archangel as he moved closer to the bed and began to strip without flicking on the lights. His shirt fell off his body, revealing that magnificent chest she'd kissed her way across more than once. Suddenly, the overwhelming weight of her emotions was gone, buried under an avalanche of gut-wrenching need.<br /><br />Raphael looked up at that moment, his gaze glittering with an earthy hunger that said he'd sensed her arousal. Deciding to save the talking for later, she was raising her fingers to tug off her own top when rain--no, hail --hit the windows in staccato bullets that made her jump. She'd have ignored it, except the hard little pellets of ice kept smashing into the glass over and over again. "Must be a storm." Dropping her hands, she walked to one of the windows after glancing over to ensure the French doors to the balcony were secure.<br /><br />Lighting flashed in vicious spikes in front of her as savage winds began to pound the house with unremitting fury, the hail turning to torrential rain between one blink and the next. "I've never seen it come in this hard, this fast."<br /><br />Raphael walked to stand beside her, his naked upper body patterned with the image of the raindrops against the window. She looked up when he didn't say anything, saw the shadows that had turned his gaze turbulent in an unexpected reflection of the storm. "What is it? What am I not seeing?" Because that look in his eyes . . .<br /><br />"What do you know of recent weather patterns across the world?"<br /><br />Elena traced a raindrop with her gaze as it tunneled across the glass. "I caught a weather update while we were at the Tower. The reporter said a tsunami had just hit the east coast of New Zealand, and that the floods in China are getting worse." Sri Lanka and the Maldives had apparently already been evacuated, but they were starting to run out of places to put people.<br /><br />"Earthquakes have been rocking Elijah's territory," Raphael told her, speaking of the South American archangel, "and he fears that at least one major volcano is about to erupt. That is not all. Michaela tells me most of Europe is shuddering in the grip of an unseasonal ice storm so vicious, it threatens to kill thousands."<br /><br />Elena's shoulder muscles went stiff at the mention of the most beautiful--and most venomous--of archangels. "The Middle East, at least," she said, forcing herself to relax, "seems to have escaped major catastrophe from what I saw on the news."<br /><br />"Yes. Favashi is helping Neha deal with the disasters in her region."<br /><br />The Archangel of Persia and the Archangel of India, Elena knew, had worked together on previous occasions. And now, when Neha hated almost everyone else in the Cadre, she seemed to be able to tolerate Favashi--perhaps because the other archangel was so much younger. "It means something, doesn't it?" she said, turning to place her hand on the wild heat of Raphael's chest, the shadowy raindrops whispering over her skin. "All this extreme weather."<br /><br />"There is a legend," Raphael murmured, his wings flaring out as he tugged her into the curve of his body--as if he would protect her. "That mountains will shake and rivers overflow, while ice creeps across the world and fields drown in rain." He looked down her at, his eyes that impossible, inhuman chrome blue. "All this will come to pass . . . when an Ancient awakens."<br /><br />The chill in his tone raised every hair on her body.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12640450483248232198"><b>5 STARS!!</b><br/><br/>Well, um, er, okay . . . how about this?<br/><br/>BIASED RATING: <b>5 STARS!!</b><br/>UNBIASED RATING: <b>3.5 STARS!</b><br/><br/><i>Phew, my conscience is clear now.</i> :-) And I can get back to my gushy, fan-girling, completely partial review . . . <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>This [...] was part of whatever it was that tied them to one another . . . that tart, twisting emotion that ripped away old scars and created new vulnerabilities in a whip of fire across the soul.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> ~SIGH~ This series is so very swoon-worthy. Nalini Singh has this amazing ab</span>
  <span id="freeText12640450483248232198" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS!!</b><br /><br />Well, um, er, okay . . . how about this?<br /><br />BIASED RATING: <b>5 STARS!!</b><br />UNBIASED RATING: <b>3.5 STARS!</b><br /><br /><i>Phew, my conscience is clear now.</i> :-) And I can get back to my gushy, fan-girling, completely partial review . . . <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>This [...] was part of whatever it was that tied them to one another . . . that tart, twisting emotion that ripped away old scars and created new vulnerabilities in a whip of fire across the soul.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> ~SIGH~ This series is so very swoon-worthy. Nalini Singh has this amazing ability to write prose that drips with intimacy and a lazy sensuality that I just cannot get enough of.<br /><br />The fact that very little happened plot-wise in this installment was of little consequence to me. I <i>savored</i> every word of Raphael and Elena's relationship. <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>He widened his stance, tucking her close enough that she nuzzled her face into his neck, one hand closing around his nape, the other continuing to caress the sensitive arch of his left wing.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> And I <i>savored</i> how every once in a while, Singh reminds the reader just how old Raphael is through either his actions or his words. <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Raphael's expression had shifted, the intimacy in those eyes stealing her breath. "You give me a memory, Consort mine. I am honored."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> And I <i>savored</i> every word of Raphael's Seven, no matter who they were interacting with. <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Venom rocked back on the balls of his feet, a slow taunting smile on his face that had Illium threatening him with dismemberment.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> I just plain <i>savored</i> this entire book. If ROMANCE is what you're looking for, look no further! <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>A shudder passed through him, his hands flexing on her hips as he tugged her to his body. "You hold me to the earth, Elena."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9875509-archangel-s-consort">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15992420-stacie?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15992420-stacie?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2846508065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16069538153375443863">4 1/2 "You're mine." Stars!<br/><br/>Once again I have fallen hard for Elena and Raphael. They are quickly becoming one of my all time favorite couples. Their push and pull; give and get is my kind of swooney. These two hold their own with each other. There is certainly physical power differences, but brute strength is not everything. True love certainly evens the field. That goes both ways...<br/><br/>However, I feel like the ending was quite anticlimactic compared to all the action that built up throughout. I was</span>
  <span id="freeText16069538153375443863" style="display:none">4 1/2 "You're mine." Stars!<br /><br />Once again I have fallen hard for Elena and Raphael. They are quickly becoming one of my all time favorite couples. Their push and pull; give and get is my kind of swooney. These two hold their own with each other. There is certainly physical power differences, but brute strength is not everything. True love certainly evens the field. That goes both ways...<br /><br />However, I feel like the ending was quite anticlimactic compared to all the action that built up throughout. I was expecting an epic battle. It was just an okay battle. That is not at al going to stop me from diving into the next book with my girls over at TPAM next month. I really do like this series a lot so far. Clearly there are some interesting characters and possibilities to explore. Happy reading!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer192595934959229762">3.5⭐<br/>I am really loving this series! So far book 1 is still my favorite, but this was still really enjoyable!   <span id="freeText192595934959229762" style="display:none">3.5⭐<br />I am really loving this series! So far book 1 is still my favorite, but this was still really enjoyable! I love being with these characters and world. It's such a unique world and take on classic paranormal archetypes. Like with book 2, I felt the the conclusion of this was slightly anti-climactic (especially since in this case it was so open ended). But I feel like this book set up some really interesting arcs for the future books! I can't wait to see how some of the things that were revealed come into play down the line! Book 4 is happening in March and I can't wait!</span>

<div id="review_1713428475" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1713428475" />
    <a title="Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed"><img alt="Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455042547p2/22911953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1713428475?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠" href="/user/show/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed">Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=machalo-august-2016-challenge">machalo-august-2016-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1713428475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14127658571412292146">Hmm, not as awesome as the previous two books. This time around it seemed like a paranormal book, whereas the others were more UF. There's not really a huge plot or mystery to solve in this book, which is why I think I didn't like it as much. This whole book's plot is about Raphael's mother and whether she's Sleeping (super hibernation coma for immortals) or not and whether she's now awakening or not. That whole is she or isn't she theme goes on the entire book and it's boring. It's too indefini</span>
  <span id="freeText14127658571412292146" style="display:none">Hmm, not as awesome as the previous two books. This time around it seemed like a paranormal book, whereas the others were more UF. There's not really a huge plot or mystery to solve in this book, which is why I think I didn't like it as much. This whole book's plot is about Raphael's mother and whether she's Sleeping (super hibernation coma for immortals) or not and whether she's now awakening or not. That whole is she or isn't she theme goes on the entire book and it's boring. It's too indefinite to be scary and not definite enough to pose a real threat. The only threat happening is super bad weather. Ok, that's not fun, and it is scary, but it's not like it's Godzilla and Mothra stalking you and trying to tear you limb from limb and then eat you like beef jerky. The big bad is too insubstantial in this book and I don't like it. <br /><br />Elena and Raphael are much more lovey dovey in this book. More sexy angel and archangel times. Elena is training and learning how to be a killing machine badass again against angels while having a giant pair of wings to worry about. Too bad they're not retractable or something. That'd really put a damper on a lot of clothing choices. Definitely spoil the lines of a lot of dresses. Raphael is getting back to ruling his city and dealing with contingency plans if his mom is insane and wanting to kill everyone when she awakens. He's his usual supportive and sexy self to Elena. <br /><br />As a whole, this book is mainly about the skeletons in Elena's and Raphael's closet. It's a book about dealing with family and that's nice and all, but it's boring. I read these books for the action and violence, not familial conflict discussions. It wasn't absent of violence, but it was more like small mishaps and murders, and it seemed tame compared to the previous two books. Here's to hoping the next book is more lively. <br /><br />More Illium, but not as much as I'd like. I hope Bluebel gets his own book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14127658571412292146" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cM3bOzKcUQU5/TWoaRb5cR+UrrifVLRIrdL3fw2ZbxzGRNLmT26mAlddnHaWcA5kvB2Es5s5d9b82pbNVnDNQA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hfkJG6dwOzNA+0MFZy0mZQn+0A4qkLqq11nFnPJOXb8zcADG2oLMNC5b6tuYS9Fwqnf6BS79eTSGUaQuqaf/4w==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer13731412981010368606">I've been writing as long as I can remember and all of my stories always held a thread of romance (even when I was writing about a prince who could shoot lasers out of his eyes). I love creating unique characters, love giving them happy endings and I even love the voices in my head. There's no other job I would rather be doing. In September 2002, when I got the call that Silhouette Desire wanted t</span>
  <span id="freeText13731412981010368606" style="display:none">I've been writing as long as I can remember and all of my stories always held a thread of romance (even when I was writing about a prince who could shoot lasers out of his eyes). I love creating unique characters, love giving them happy endings and I even love the voices in my head. There's no other job I would rather be doing. In September 2002, when I got the call that Silhouette Desire wanted to buy my first book, Desert Warrior, it was a dream come true. I hope to continue living the dream until I keel over of old age on my keyboard.<br /><br /><br />I was born in Fiji and raised in New Zealand. I also spent three years living and working in Japan, during which time I took the chance to travel around Asia. I’m back in New Zealand now, but I’m always plotting new trips. If you’d like to see some of my travel snapshots, have a look at the Travel Diary page (updated every month).<br /><br />So far, I've worked as a lawyer, a librarian, a candy factory general hand, a bank temp and an English teacher and not necessarily in that order. Some might call that inconsistency but I call it grist for the writer's mill.<br /><br /></span>

"Husband" was too human, "partner" factually wrong for a being as powerful as an archangel, "mate"...perhaps. But none of it was quite right. "Mine," she said at last.<br /><br />He blinked and when he raised his lashes again, the blue was liquid fire. <i>Yes, that will do.</i> "But for public consumption, you are my consort."<br /><br />"Consort," she murmured, tasting the word, feeling it's shape. "Yes, that fits.&rdquo;</span>
